The approach:
1. Reduce `recheck_fallback_worker` sleep from 30s to 3s
2. Parallelize the demotion and promotion checks using `FuturesUnordered`

But there's also an issue: with 32 modems, even parallel `AT+CPIN?` commands every 3 seconds is a lot of AT traffic. 

The real problem is that the 30-second timer is the bottleneck here. I could optimize by only checking modems that are actually relevant—SIM-bearing modems for demotion checks and fallback modems for promotion checks—but with 32 modems most likely having SIMs, I'd still be querying nearly all of them every 3 seconds, which is a lot of traffic.

The most practical solution is to split this into two approaches: keep the existing 30-second cycle for the main logic, then add a faster, separate worker that specifically targets just the fallback modems (checking for SIM insertion) and recently promoted active modems. Or even simpler—just reduce the sleep interval to 3 seconds and parallelize all the checks, since they should respond quickly anyway.

I'm also wondering if there's a URC-based approach that could help here, where the modem itself notifies us of state changes rather than us constantly polling.

Actually, the E25 modem does send `+CPIN: READY` and `+CPIN: NOT READY` as unsolicited result codes when the SIM status changes, but our current architecture doesn't have a URC reader—we only read from the serial port in response to commands. Adding that would require significant refactoring.

So the practical path forward is to reduce the sleep to 3 seconds and parallelize both the fallback and demotion checks using `FuturesUnordered`. For the demotion check specifically, I need to collect all the demotions first before applying them to the HashMap, since I can't write to it while iterating.

## 1. **`initialize_single_modem` in manager.rs — Error Handling**

[src/modem/manager.rs](src/modem/manager.rs#L79-L117):
```rust
async fn initialize_single_modem(
    port: String,
    baud_rate: u32,
    device_id: String,
    sms_storage: Option<SmsStorage>,
    index: usize,
) -> anyhow::Result<(String, Modem, bool)> {
    info!("Initializing modem on port {}", port);

    let modem = Modem::new(&port, baud_rate, &device_id, index).await?;  // Fails here if port can't open
    
    // ... rest of init
    
    Ok((sim_id, modem, is_new_sim))
}
```

**Behavior:**
- If `Modem::new()` fails (port not found, access denied, etc.), the `?` operator returns `Err` immediately
- **Failed modems do NOT appear in the HashMap at all**
- The error is caught in [lines 47-50](src/modem/manager.rs#L47-L50) of `initialize()`:
```rust
Err(e) => {
    error!("Failed to initialize modem: {}", e);
    failed_count += 1;
}
```
- Failed ports are completely skipped; they don't get added to the `modems` HashMap

## 2. **`Modem::new()` in core.rs — Serial Port Failure**

[src/modem/core.rs](src/modem/core.rs#L46-L47):
```rust
pub async fn new(com_port: &str, baud_rate: u32, name: &str, index: usize) -> io::Result<Self> {
    let serial_stream = Self::create_serial_connection(com_port, baud_rate).await?;
```

**Error Type & Message:**
- Returns `io::Result<Self>` (equivalent to `Result<Self, std::io::Error>`)
- If port can't be opened, `create_serial_connection()` fails with an `io::Error`
- The `?` operator propagates this error immediately
- Typical error messages: `"Permission denied"`, `"No such file or directory"`, etc. (OS-level errors)

[src/modem/core.rs](src/modem/core.rs#L103-L108):
```rust
async fn create_serial_connection(
    com_port: &str,
    baud_rate: u32,
) -> tokio_serial::Result<SerialStream> {
    tokio_serial::new(com_port, baud_rate)
        .timeout(Duration::from_secs(10))
        .flow_control(tokio_serial::FlowControl::None)
        .open_native_async()
```

## 5. **`initialize_all_modems` — Failed Modem Collection**

[src/modem/manager.rs](src/modem/manager.rs#L42-L56):
```rust
let mut modems = HashMap::new();
let mut new_sim_ids = Vec::new();
let mut failed_count = 0;

while let Some(result) = initialization_futures.next().await {
    match result {
        Ok((sim_id, modem, is_new)) => {
            if is_new {
                new_sim_ids.push(sim_id.clone());
            }
            modems.insert(sim_id, Arc::new(modem));
        }
        Err(e) => {
            error!("Failed to initialize modem: {}", e);
            failed_count += 1;  // Only counted, not stored
        }
    }
}
```

**Answer:**
- **Failed ports are NOT collected anywhere** — only a counter is incremented
- Failed modems are **completely absent from the final HashMap**
- If no modems succeed, the entire initialization fails ([line 57-59](src/modem/manager.rs#L57-L59)):
```rust
if modems.is_empty() {
    return Err(anyhow::anyhow!("No modems were successfully initialized"));
}
```

### **1. API ENDPOINT**

**Location**: [src/api/mod.rs](src/api/mod.rs#L203)

**Route & Handler**: `POST /api/sms` → `send_sms()` (line 203–230)

**Request Payload** ([SmsPayload](src/api/mod.rs#L562), line 562):
```rust
pub struct SmsPayload {
    sim_id: String,      // Modem/SIM identifier
    contact: Contact,    // {id: String, name: String}
    message: String,     // SMS plaintext (max 500 chars enforced by frontend)
    new: bool,          // If true, auto-create contact
}
```

**Response** (line 222–223):
- **Success (200 OK)**: `{"sms_id": i64, "contact_id": String}`
- **Error (500)**: `"Send failed: {error_message}"`

**Handler Logic** (lines 203–230):
1. If `new=true`, calls `payload.contact.find_or_create()` to insert contact into DB
2. Calls `modem_manager.send_sms(sim_id, contact, message)` 
3. **On success**: broadcasts conversation via `sse_manager.send(convs)`, returns sms_id & contact_id
4. **On error**: returns 500 with error string
5. **⚠️ No retry logic at this layer**

---

### **2. MODEM-LEVEL SEND LOGIC**

#### **Manager Layer**
**Location**: [src/modem/manager.rs](src/modem/manager.rs#L178)  
**Function**: `send_sms()` (line 178–191)
- Routes request to correct modem instance by `sim_id`
- Delegates to `modem.send_sms_pdu(contact, message)` 
- Returns `(sms_id, contact_id)` or error

#### **Core PDU Send Path**
**Location**: [src/modem/core.rs](src/modem/core.rs#L471)

**`send_sms_pdu()`** (line 471–503):
- Creates DB record with `Sms::insert()` → `status = Loading`
- Calls internal `send_pdu_message(phone, message)` 
- **On success**: `Sms::update_status_by_id(sms_id, Read)`
- **On error**: `Sms::update_status_by_id(sms_id, Failed)`, propagates error

**`send_pdu_message()`** (line 504–511):
1. Calls `build_pdu(phone, message)` → returns `(pdu_hex: String, tpdu_length: usize)`
2. Calls `send_sms_content(&format!("AT+CMGS={}\r", tpdu_length), pdu_data, |pdu| Ok(pdu))`

**`send_sms_content()`** (line 440–469) - Generic SMS wrapper:
1. Send `AT+CMGS=<length>` via priority queue
2. Wait for `"> "` prompt (ready for input)
3. Transform message via closure (identity for PDU, UCS2 encoding for text)
4. Append Ctrl+Z (0x1A) and send
5. Parse response for `"OK\r\n"` + `"+CMGS:"` (message reference number)
6. **Error handling**: If response incomplete → log, return `Err("Incomplete SMS response")`

#### **PDU Encoding**
**Location**: [src/modem/pdu.rs](src/modem/pdu.rs#L63)

**`build_pdu(mobile, message)`** (line 63–67):
- Returns: `(full_pdu_hex_string, tpdu_length_in_bytes)`
- Prepends SMSC info: `"00"` (use default service center)
- Appends encoded TPDU

**`encode_tpdu(mobile, message)`** (line 39–58) - GSM PDU construction:
```
FIRST_OCTET: "11"              // Send SMS, request status report
MESSAGE_REF: "00"              // Message reference
DESTINATION: <phone_encoded>   // Length + addr_type + BCD-swapped digits
PID: "00"                       // Protocol ID (standard SMS)
DCS: "08"                       // Data Coding Scheme (UCS2)
VP: "00"                        // Validity Period (default)
UDL: <message.chars().count() * 2>  // User Data Length (UCS2 = 2 bytes/char)
UD: <ucs2_hex_encoded_message>  // User Data
```

**Phone Processing** ([parse_number()](src/modem/pdu.rs#L18)):
- Strip leading `+`, remove spaces
- Addr type: `0x91` if international (+), else `0x81` (national)
- Swap digit pairs (BCD format): "1234" → "2143"
- Pad with 'F' if odd length

**Message Encoding** ([string_to_ucs2()](src/modem/pdu.rs#L1)):
- UTF-16 big-endian encode
- **Limit: 70 characters max** (UCS2 = 140 bytes)
- Error if exceeded: `"UCS2 message too long (max 70 characters), current: {n}"`
- Return hex-encoded bytes

#### **AT Command Execution & Retry**
**Location**: [src/modem/core.rs](src/modem/core.rs#L140)

**`execute_command_with_retry()`** (line 140–199):
- Max retries: `MAX_RETRIES` (likely 3)
- Retry condition: **ONLY on `NotConnected` error** (not on send failures)
- Retry delay: `RETRY_DELAY = Duration::from_millis(500)`
- Other errors: sent immediately, no retry
- Max retries exceeded → return `Err("Maximum retries exceeded")`

**`execute_single_command()`** (line 262–301):
- Sends raw AT command to serial port
- Reads response with **8-second timeout**
- Expected terminators: `"OK\r\n"`, `"ERROR\r\n"`, `"+CME ERROR:"`, `"+CMS ERROR:"`, `">"`
- Picks latest terminator in buffer
- On timeout: `Err("Command timeout for device {name}")`

### **3. FRONTEND SEND UI**

#### **Send Dialog Component**
**Location**: [frontend/src/components/message/SendDialog.svelte](frontend/src/components/message/SendDialog.svelte#L1)

**Form Fields** (lines 74–135):
1. **SIM Dropdown** (lines 74–88):
   - Binds to `selectedSim`
   - Display: `simCard.alias || simCard.phone_number || simCard.id.slice(-8)`
   - From store: `$simCards`

2. **Recipient Phone** (lines 90–104):
   - Type: `tel` input
   - Validation regex: `/^\d{7,15}$/` (7–15 digits only)
   - Binds to `recipient`

3. **Message Content** (lines 106–120):
   - Type: `textarea`
   - Max length: **500 characters**
   - Binds to `message`
   - Placeholder: "请输入消息内容（最多500字）"

4. **Action Buttons** (lines 122–135):
   - Cancel: closes dialog
   - Send: disabled while `isLoading`, shows "发送中..." while sending

#### **Client-Side Validation** (lines 57–64):
```javascript
const validateForm = () => {
    error = "";
    if (!selectedSim)                      error = "请选择SIM卡";
    else if (!/^\d{7,15}$/.test(recipient)) error = "请输入有效的电话号码";
    else if (!message.trim())              error = "请输入消息内容";
    return !error;
};
```
- **Enforced**: SIM selection, 7–15 digit phone, non-empty message
- **⚠️ No character encoding validation** (500 char limit applies to frontend only)

#### **Submit Handler** (lines 47–56):
```javascript
const handleSubmit = async () => {
    if (!validateForm()) return;
    isLoading = true;
    try {
        await apiClient.sendSms(selectedSim, recipient, message);
        close();
    } catch (err) {
        error = err.message || "发送失败，请稍后重试";  // Generic error
    } finally {
        isLoading = false;
    }
};
```
- **No retry logic** — single attempt
- **Error display**: Generic Chinese message, no details from backend

#### **API Client**
**Location**: [frontend/src/js/api.js](frontend/src/js/api.js#L45)

```javascript
async sendSms(simId, contact, message, new_message) {
    const payload = { sim_id: simId, contact, message, new: new_message };
    return FetchApi.post('/api/sms', payload)
}
```
- Simple wrapper, no additional validation
- Returns: response data on 200, throws on error

#### **Message List Integration**
**Location**: [frontend/src/components/message/MessageList.svelte](frontend/src/components/message/MessageList.svelte#L153)

**Send flow** (lines 153–179):
1. Create optimistic message: `status = SmsStatus.Loading`, `id = -1`
2. Call `apiClient.sendSms(simId, concat, newMessage.message, $currentContact.new)`
3. **On success**:
   - Update optimistic message: set `id = res.data.sms_id`, `status = SmsStatus.Read`
4. **On error**:
   - Update optimistic message: `status = SmsStatus.Failed`
   - Log to console: `console.error("发送消息失败:", err)`
   - **⚠️ No user notification beyond error state**
5. Update conversation last message timestamp

---

### **4. VALIDATION & ERROR HANDLING**

| Layer | Type | Coverage | Details |
|-------|------|----------|---------|
| **Frontend** | Input | Strict | Phone 7–15 digits, message 500 chars max |
| **Backend DB** | Creation | Partial | Contact auto-created only if `new=true` |
| **PDU Encoding** | Message | Hard | UCS2 max 70 chars; exceeding is fatal error |
| **Serial** | Timeout | Yes | 8-second per-command timeout |
| **AT Command** | Retry | Limited | Retry only on `NotConnected`, NOT on send failures |
| **Status Tracking** | State | Yes | Sms.status: Unread(0), Read(1), **Loading(2), Failed(3)** |
| **API Response** | HTTP | Yes | 500 error on any send failure |

**Status Update Path**: [src/db.rs](src/db.rs#L292)  
`Sms::update_status_by_id(id, status)` (line 292–305)

---

### **5. GAPS & MISSING FEATURES**

| Gap | Impact | Priority |
|-----|--------|----------|
| **No API-level retry** | Transient modem errors (timeout, disconnection) NOT retried; user must manually re-send | High |
| **No real-time status updates** | Frontend doesn't receive send completion (success/fail) after 200 response; SSE only broadcasts conversation, not individual SMS state | High |
| **No delivery confirmation** | Failed sends are set to Failed status in DB but NOT communicated back to frontend in real-time | High |
| **No GSM-7 encoding** | Always uses UCS2 (inefficient); English ASCII messages waste bandwidth (70 chars in UCS2 vs 160 in GSM-7) | Medium |
| **No deduplication tracking** | Vulnerable to accidental double-sends if user clicks Send twice | Medium |
| **No rate limiting** | No per-SIM, per-recipient, or per-user rate limits; susceptible to SMS flooding attacks | Medium |
| **Message validation only at PDU encoding** | UCS2 max 70 char limit is hard-coded deep in PDU function; frontend 500 char limit is arbitrary and decoupled | Low |
| **No message queue/persistence** | If backend crashes mid-send, no recovery; no job queue for offline modems | Medium |
| **No contact phone validation** | `Contact.name` field can contain any string; no validation that it matches actual phone number | Low |
| **No conversation update on new send** | New contacts created with UUID but not linked to send recipient in conversation UI; chat history not auto-opened | Low |

**Steps**

**1. [frontend/src/App.svelte](frontend/src/App.svelte)** — Add `currentPage` state and pass `onNavigate` to both pages. Replace the entire `<script>` block and the `{#if $isAuthenticated}` section:

```svelte
<script>
  // add after existing imports:
  let currentPage = $state('sim');
</script>

<!-- replace the {#if $isAuthenticated} block with: -->
{#if $isAuthenticated}
  {#if currentPage === 'sim'}
    <div in:fly={{ x: -50, duration: 400, easing: quartOut }} out:fly={{ x: 50, duration: 300, easing: quartOut }}>
      <SimDashboard onNavigate={() => (currentPage = 'messages')} />
    </div>
  {:else}
    <div in:fly={{ x: 50, duration: 400, easing: quartOut }} out:fly={{ x: -50, duration: 300, easing: quartOut }}>
      <Dashboard onNavigate={() => (currentPage = 'sim')} />
    </div>
  {/if}
```

The user wants to call `AT+QCPBMPREF=1` before `AT+CNUM`. This is a Quectel-specific command that sets the phonebook memory preference to SIM (rather than ME/modem memory), which ensures `AT+CNUM` reads from the SIM card.

The `get_phone_number` function currently just sends `AT+CNUM`. I need to modify it to:
1. First send `AT+QCPBMPREF=1` (set phonebook memory preference to SIM)
2. Then send `AT+CNUM`

However, since `get_phone_number` is called in parallel with `get_sim_iccid` and `get_sim_imsi` via `tokio::join!`, I need to be careful. The `AT+QCPBMPREF=1` needs to complete before `AT+CNUM`, but both are sequential within `get_phone_number` itself.


Since all three functions run in parallel through `tokio::join!` in `init_sim_info`, the command queue will handle them sequentially anyway, so sending `AT+QCPBMPREF=1` first within `get_phone_number` won't cause issues with the other commands running concurrently. and `AT+CNUM` will execute in sequence within that same future, so there's no race condition to worry about.

--- ASSISTANT ---
`AT+QCPBMPREF=1` sets the phonebook memory preference to SIM (rather than modem internal storage) before `AT+CNUM` reads from it. I'll update `get_phone_number` to send it first:

Now I can see the issue clearly. The `parse_pdu_sms` function doesn't check the PDU type (MTI - Message Type Indicator). For SUBMIT PDUs (sent messages stored by the modem):

- PDU type byte: bit 0-1 = 01 (SUBMIT)
- After PDU type: **Message Reference** (1 byte) - THIS IS MISSING IN THE PARSER
- Then TP-DA (Destination Address, which is the recipient, NOT the sender)
- Then PID, DCS
- Then **Validity Period** (VP, variable length) - NOT timestamp for DELIVER


- Then TP-UDL and the message content

For DELIVER PDUs (received messages), the structure is different:
- PDU type byte: bit 0-1 = 00 (DELIVER)
- After PDU type: TP-OA (Originating Address = sender)
- Then PID, DCS
- Then **SCTS** (timestamp, 7 bytes)
- Then TP-UDL and the message content

So when the parser encounters a SUBMIT PDU with type `0x11` (SUBMIT with relative VP), it's skipping the Message Reference byte and misinterpreting the Destination Address as the sender, which is why the numbers are appearing in the wrong field.

Parsing the timestamp... So after the SUBMIT PDUs get parsed and deleted from the modem, they won't interfere anymore—the real received SMS should come through normally on the next cycle. But I'm realizing the parser might actually crash when it tries to extract the timestamp from a SUBMIT PDU, since the structure is different and could cause an index out of bounds panic. This could cause the parse thread to crash!

Let me check: for a SUBMIT PDU with Validity Period Format (VPF) = 10 (relative VP, 1 byte), the structure after PID is:
- DCS (1 byte)
- VP (1 byte for relative)
- UDL (1 byte)
- UD

So after `parse_sender` (wrong position anyway) and PID and DCS:
- pos points to VP (1 byte for relative VP)
- `parse_timestamp(&pdu[pos..pos + 7])` tries to read 7 bytes starting at VP

If pdu.len() < pos + 7, this panics! This would kill the spawned task processing this SMS read!

If VPF = 10 (relative VP), VP is only 1 byte. After DCS comes VP (1 byte), UDL (1 byte), then the actual message data. For something like a 5-character message in UCS2 encoding, that's 10 bytes of payload, so we'd have 12 bytes minimum after DCS. But with a very short message—just 1 character encoded as 2 bytes—we're looking at only VP (1) + UDL (1) + UD (2) = 4 bytes, which means the buffer could easily be too small for that 7-byte read.

The panic happens inside `parse_pdu_sms`, which is called from `read_sms`. When the panic occurs, it crashes the tokio task handling SMS for that modem port, and the error propagates back through `read_sms_async_insert`. the panic would propagate up and crash the entire `read_sms_worker` task, stopping all SMS reading. The root cause is that `parse_pdu_sms` tries to read a 7-byte timestamp from SUBMIT PDUs that are too short, causing a buffer overflow panic that kills the worker.

```rust
fn parse_sender(pdu: &[u8], pos: &mut usize) -> String {
    let sender_len = pdu[*pos] as usize;  // reads byte as length
    *pos += 1;
    let sender_type = pdu[*pos];  // reads next byte as type
```

--- ASSISTANT ---
Yes, exactly. There are two detection paths in `recheck_fallback_modems()`:

**1. SIM removed then re-inserted (different SIM):**
- `AT+CPIN?` returns not-READY → modem demoted to `fallback_sim_N`
- Next recheck cycle: `AT+CCID` returns a new ICCID → modem promoted with the new ICCID as the map key

**2. Direct SIM swap (old SIM pulled, new SIM inserted so fast that `+CPIN?` is already READY):**
```rust
if let Ok(Some(current_iccid)) = modem.get_sim_iccid().await {
    if current_iccid != iccid {  // ← map key vs live AT+CCID response
        // Force demotion + re-init
    }
}
```

So in both cases, the ICCID mismatch between the map key (old SIM) and the live `AT+CCID` response (new SIM) is what triggers re-initialization. The new ICCID becomes the new map key after promotion.

--- ASSISTANT (thinking) ---
The user is asking whether AT+CPIN? is necessary for SIM swap detection, given that AT+CCID already reveals ICCID changes.

Looking at the code, there are actually two separate purposes for AT+CPIN?:

1. **SIM removal detection (demotion)**: When a SIM is physically removed, `AT+CPIN?` returns not-READY (no SIM), which triggers demotion to `fallback_sim_N`. `AT+CCID` in this case would return an error or empty — so you could also use that.

2. **Direct SIM swap detection**: When one SIM is swapped for another quickly, `AT+CPIN?` still returns READY (new SIM is ready), so the code then falls through to check ICCID mismatch.


So theoretically, I could consolidate this into a single `AT+CCID` check: if it returns an error or None, demote the SIM; if it returns a different ICCID, demote and reinitialize with the new one. Both removal and swap scenarios would be covered by just comparing the ICCID.

--- ASSISTANT ---
Correct — `AT+CPIN?` is redundant. A single `AT+CCID` check covers both cases:

| Scenario | `AT+CCID` result | Action needed |
|---|---|---|
| SIM removed | returns `None`/error | Demote to fallback |
| Direct SIM swap | returns different ICCID | Demote + re-init |
| Same SIM still present | returns same ICCID | Do nothing |

Currently the code does two serial AT commands per modem per recheck cycle (`AT+CPIN?` → then conditionally `AT+CCID`). You could replace both with a single `AT+CCID` call:

```rust
// Instead of: get_sim_status() then get_sim_iccid()
// Just do: get_sim_iccid()

match modem.get_sim_iccid().await {
    Ok(Some(current_iccid)) if current_iccid == iccid => None, // same SIM, no action
    Ok(Some(current_iccid)) => Some((iccid, fallback_key, com_port)), // swap detected
    _ => Some((iccid, fallback_key, com_port)), // removed or error → demote
}
```

This halves the AT command traffic on the demotion check path. The only theoretical reason to keep `AT+CPIN?` would be if `AT+CCID` behaves differently on some modem firmware when no SIM is present (e.g., hangs instead of returning an error), but for EC20F that's not a concern.

Now for multipart messages I need to set TP-UDHI to 1, so I'm ORing 0x11 with 0x40 to get 0x51. Let me verify this breaks down correctly: 0x51 in binary is 0b01010001, which gives me TP-MTI = 01 (SUBMIT), RD = 0, VPF = 10 (relative), and SRR = 0 as expected.

For the UDH structure, I'm building a 6-byte header starting with the length field, then the information element identifier for concatenated messages, followed by the element length and three data bytes for the reference number, total segment count, and current segment index.

--- ASSISTANT (thinking) ---
The user is asking how the `cargo test pdu` tests work without needing a real COM port. This is a conceptual question about why the unit tests don't need COM ports.

--- ASSISTANT ---
The tests don't need a COM port because `pdu.rs` is **pure encoding logic** — it just transforms strings into hex PDU strings. No serial port, no AT commands, no hardware involved at all.

The phone number in the test (e.g. `"+8618126101015"`) is only used to encode the **destination address field** inside the PDU hex string. The test never opens a COM port or sends anything — it just checks the output string is correctly formatted.

The COM port is only touched in `core.rs` → `send_sms_content()`, which writes the PDU to the serial port. That layer is separate and can't be unit-tested without real hardware (or a mock).

So the split is:

| Layer | Testable without hardware? |
|---|---|
| `pdu.rs` — encode message → hex string | ✅ Yes, pure functions |
| `core.rs` — write hex to COM port | ❌ Needs real modem or mock |
| `manager.rs` — route by SIM ID | ❌ Needs real modem or mock |

`cargo test pdu` only exercises the first layer. That's intentional — you can verify the PDU encoding is correct (segment count, UDH format, first octet flags) without any hardware at all.
